>
> **[6:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-broad-world-of-azure-services?u=76281980&t=372)** You can set up Windows 10 or Windows 11 desktops, or your employees access them from the Azure Virtual Desktop client.
>
> **[6:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-broad-world-of-azure-services?u=76281980&t=378)** And then finally at the very bottom, we have the web category.
>
> **[6:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-broad-world-of-azure-services?u=76281980&t=382)** So here you find things like Azure Functions, which you can call from your web application.
>
> **[6:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-broad-world-of-azure-services?u=76281980&t=387)** Here we have our web apps.
>
> **[6:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-broad-world-of-azure-services?u=76281980&t=388)** We have web apps for containers.
>
> **[6:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-broad-world-of-azure-services?u=76281980&t=390)** We can do static web apps.
>
> **[6:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-broad-world-of-azure-services?u=76281980&t=392)** We can set up notification hubs to push notifications across web applications and web APIs.
>
> **[6:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-broad-world-of-azure-services?u=76281980&t=398)** So this is where you find your web-specific tools.
>
> **[6:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-broad-world-of-azure-services?u=76281980&t=400)** As you can see, there is a wide range of tools and capabilities available in Azure.
>
> **[6:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-broad-world-of-azure-services?u=76281980&t=406)** Have fun exploring.

### 3. Azure App Service

#### A quick tour of Azure app service
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Azure App Service is a cornerstone of Microsoft Azure's cloud offerings.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=4)** It acts as a virtual web server in the cloud.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=7)** It provides a robust and scalable platform for developers to build, deploy, and manage web applications, APIs, serverless functions, logic apps, and mobile back-ends.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=18)** Whenever you connect to a website, your browser connects to a web server.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=21)** A web server, as many of you might know, is a specialized computer system or software application that handles requests from clients, typically web browsers or other software applications, and responds by delivering the requested webpages or data.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=35)** This process involves several critical components, including server hardware, operating systems, networking protocols, and server-side software.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=43)** The location and nature of these servers has evolved significantly over the years.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=48)** Initially, servers might have been in simple boxes in a company closet.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=52)** Soon, they were in huge data centers.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=54)** However, the evolution from those simple setups to extensive server farms is not over.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=59)** Now we have the option of getting them on Azure.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=62)** For a company looking to publish an application, a website, or an API to the internet, acquiring a web server is a fundamental step.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=70)** This can involve choosing between hosting solutions, such as shared hosting, virtual private servers, dedicated servers, or cloud-based solutions.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=79)** Each of these options offers varying levels of control, performance, and cost, allowing the business to select the best fit for their needs.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=87)** Setting up a web server also requires considerations for security, scalability, and maintenance, ensuring that the server can handle traffic efficiently and remain secure against potential threats.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=98)** As your app service falls into the cloud category and provides all the necessary tools to make it easy to deploy and manage your web applications, APIs, and other project, it serves as your virtual web server in the cloud.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=110)** There are several choices available for publishing to the internet.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=113)** In the Microsoft cloud, the Azure App Service is the best choice for most web apps and services, and is the focus of this chapter.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=120)** It stands out as a robust and scalable solution.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=123)** It allows businesses to quickly deploy, manage, and scale web applications and APIs on a fully managed platform, providing high availability and security features without the need for extensive infrastructure management.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=135)** Service Fabric is a good choice if you're creating a new app or rewriting an existing app to use microservice architecture.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=142)** Service Fabric makes it easy to develop, package, deploy, and manage containerized and non-containerized microservices.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=150)** If you really want to manage your own service, use Azure Virtual Machines or the Azure Container tools.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=155)** If you are considering this, you are responsible for correctly configuring and securing the VM or container.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=161)** Plus, you must be diligent in patching and updating the environment.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=164)** Check out some other videos in this course to learn more about Azure VMs.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=168)** To clarify where each of these options stands in the service areas, virtual machines is infrastructure as a service, while App Service and Service Fabric are platform as a service, Azure App Service is a fully managed platform as a service offering.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=182)** Let's review what platform as a service means.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=185)** It is a complete development and deployment environment in the cloud.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=189)** You focus on creating the application.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=191)** The platform, in this case, Azure App Service, takes care of building the infrastructure, handling all the messy web protocols and networking pieces, so there is a robust location for your app.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=202)** Plus, it integrates with development tools and makes it easy to publish your app to the cloud.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=207)** Going beyond the capabilities of a traditional web server, Azure App Service offers automatic scaling, seamless integration with other Azure services and support from multiple programming languages.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=218)** Furthermore, it handles infrastructure management automatically, allowing developers to focus solely on their applications.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=224)** Web applications and web APIs are obvious types of apps for a cloud web service.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=228)** This platform as a service is a convenient way to get systems ready for web project.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=232)** It's so convenient that other teams at Microsoft have also chosen it as their platform.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=236)** For example, Logic Apps and Azure Functions run on it.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=239)** It supports a wide range of server-side programming languages, and frameworks.

>

>

>

#### Build a new app service

### 4. APIs and API Management

#### Host Web APIs on app service
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] API applications are another type of web component that is hosted on a web server.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=4)** Web APIs have a programmatic interface that can be used by other applications.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=9)** Developers write apps or websites that use the API.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=12)** For example, it's possible to post a tweet using the Twitter API.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=16)** In Azure, these were once called Azure API apps.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=19)** Now they are just another site that can be hosted in an app service.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=22)** An API app will run in the app service.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=24)** So we start out the same.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=25)** Provision of service plan and add an app service to the plan.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=29)** Now you've got an empty app service.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=30)** This next step is we need to create content and deploy it to the app service.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=34)** There are two parts to our API app, the app service we've provisioned.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=37)** Then we need to build the API code.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=39)** Most APIs today are REST based, so we would need to code a REST component that does the work of the API.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=45)** An API app can be developed in any technology that you can use to develop a REST API, such [ASB.NET](https://ASB.NET), Java, PHP, and other languages.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=54)** While the documentation on Azure implies that there are some extra features available for API apps and app services, that's not a very accurate portrayal.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=62)** There are some API templates available in Azure to jumpstart the project, but as far as what Azure provides, web apps and APIs are virtually identical on the Azure site.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=72)** However, there are some features that can help API apps.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=75)** For example, it would be helpful to use Swagger, also known as OpenAPI, to document the API interface.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=82)** That way our API clients can discover more about the API before using it, but this is something that you'd build into your app code, not something that is provided by Azure.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=91)** One necessary feature that is part of Azure App Service is CORS.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=95)** CORS is an HTTP feature that enables a web application running under one domain to access resources in another domain.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=102)** Web browsers implement a security restriction known as same origin policy that prevents a webpage from calling APIs in different domains.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=110)** CORS provides a secure way to allow one domain, the origin domain, to call APIs in another domain.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=115)** This is useful and Azure does support CORS, but it's not an API specific feature.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=120)** It can be added to any app service.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=122)** Finally, it's common nowadays for companies to build lots of APIs and microservices.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/host-web-apis-on-app-service?u=76281980&t=127)** In the next video, we'll look at Azure API Management Tools.

### 5. Code and Workflows

#### Run serverless code with Azure Functions
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Azure functions is a solution for easily running small pieces of code in the cloud.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=5)** You can write just the code you need for the problem at hand without worrying about creating a whole application or building the infrastructure to run it.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=14)** Azure Functions is a serverless compute service that lets you run event driven code without needing to provision or manage servers.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=22)** Despite the term, serverless, servers are still involved.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=26)** However, the responsibility of managing these servers and infrastructure falls on the cloud provider, not the end user.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=33)** The compute resources are allocated dynamically and automatically scaled to meet varying demands.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=38)** This means the server runs only when the code is executed.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=42)** Serverless doesn't mean no server, but rather less server, as servers run only when needed.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=48)** You can write your function code in your preferred language using your favorite development tools, and then deploy your code to the Azure Cloud.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=56)** You can write your code in any of these languages.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=59)** Azure function supports a variety of languages and their respective package managers.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=63)** Azure function supports NuGet and npm.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=66)** It supports PIP and Maven, so you can use your favorite libraries.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=70)** You can include these packages in your Azure Functions project, and they will be deployed along with your function app.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=77)** If you're using a package that isn't included in the standard library of your chosen language, you need to include it in your project's dependencies.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=85)** Azure also offers Azure Artifacts, a universal package management service that lets you create, host, and share packages with your team.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=94)** This service is part of the Azure DevOps family.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=97)** If you want to learn more, I have a course on this topic in the LinkedIn learning catalog.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=102)** The main advantage of Azure Functions is its simplicity and cost effectiveness.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=106)** It allows you to write less code, maintain less infrastructure, and save on costs.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=112)** Instead of worrying about deploying and maintaining servers, the cloud infrastructure provides all the up-to-date resources needed to keep your applications running.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=120)** A function remains idle until it is requested to execute, triggered by an event known as a trigger.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=126)** Each function can only have one trigger.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=129)** Triggers typically carry data associated with the event often provided as the function's payload.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=134)** There are a bunch of triggers that can kick off the action.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=137)** There's the HTTPTrigger, useful for starting the execution of your code upon an HTTP request.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=144)** A TimerTrigger is used to execute the function on a predefined schedule.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=148)** There's a database-specific trigger called the CosmosDBTrigger.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=152)** This triggers when Azure Cosmos DB processes documents when they're added or updated in the collections in one of their NoSQL databases.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=160)** When Azure Storage blobs are added to containers that triggers the BlobTrigger.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=165)** You might use this function for image resizing.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=167)** You can respond to messages as they arrive in an Azure Storage queue using the QueueTrigger.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=172)** Input and output bindings provide a declarative way to connect to data within your code.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=177)** Bindings are optional and a function can have multiple input and output bindings.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=182)** An input binding represents data sent to the function, while the output binding represents data passed out of the function.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=189)** Think of binding as a way to integrate with other Azure services.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=193)** Triggers and bindings help you avoid hard coding service details.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=197)** Your function receives data through the parameters and sends data using its return value.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=202)** For example, I've used function bindings with Power Automate to extract A URL from the content of an email.

>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=224)** The hosting option impacts how your function app is scaled and the resources available to each function app instance.
>
> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=230)** The basic one, the simplest one, is the consumption plan.

> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=234)** You pay only when your function runs with automatic scaling based on incoming events.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=239)** Next is the flex consumption plan, which offers high scalability with pre-provisioned instances and virtual networking for security.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=247)** The premium plan provides pre-warmed workers for immediate execution, more control over instances and extended capabilities.
>
> **[4:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=254)** The dedicated plan runs functions within an app service plan, ideal for predictable billing and long-running scenarios.

> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/run-serverless-code-with-azure-functions?u=76281980&t=261)** And then finally, we have the container apps, deploys containerized functions apps in a managed environment, avoiding Kubernetes complexity and supporting high-end processing power.

#### Building powerful workflows with logic apps
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Presenter] Azure Logic Apps and Power Automate are both powerful services provided by Microsoft that excel at automating business workflows.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=8)** Azure Logic Apps targets IT professionals and developers, whereas Power Automate is designed for business users and citizen developers.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=16)** A citizen developer in this context refers to a non-professional developer who creates applications or automates workflows using tools that require little or no coding knowledge.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=25)** Power Automate provides a user-friendly and focused-experience within Microsoft 365.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=30)** Azure Logic Apps is a cloud service that helps you schedule, automate and orchestrate tasks, business processes and workflows when you need to integrate apps, data, systems, and services across enterprises and organizations.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=42)** Power Automate is built on top of Azure Logic apps and shares much of the same architecture in a common set of connectors.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=49)** Azure Logic Apps is more focused on business needs that span data centers.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=53)** Think of it as a super set of power automate.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=55)** It is built on serverless principles and has a containerized runtime in the backend.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=61)** A Logic App workflow is a series of steps that automate a business process.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=65)** It starts with a trigger, such as receiving an email or a new file being added to a folder, and then performs a sequence of actions based on that trigger.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=74)** These actions can include tasks like sending notifications, updating databases, or integrating with other services.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=80)** The workflow is designed using a visual interface, making it easy to connect different tasks and services without needing to write code.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=87)** Let's look at some examples.

> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=88)** We could create a Logic app that moves uploaded files from an FTP server into Azure Storage.

>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=106)** When the truck driver drops off or picks up loads, they touch a button in the app, which alerts Logic apps to create the EDI document and send it to the retailer.
>

> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=136)** Every Logic app has one or more connectors.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=139)** A connector provides one or more prebuilt operations, which you use as steps in your workflow.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=144)** Azure provides hundreds of connectors, triggers, and prebuilt templates, making automation of mundane and mission critical tasks easy.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=151)** A connector is a proxy or a wrapper around an API that allows the underlying service to talk to Power automate, and logic apps.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=159)** Each connector provides one or more prebuilt operations. In a connector, each operation is either a trigger operation that starts a workflow or an action operation that performs a specific task.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=172)** In addition, operations have configurable properties that add context to the workflow.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=177)** Currently, there are over 200 connectors.

> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=205)** All logic apps start with a trigger which defines the events that initiate and start a workflow.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=210)** This could be when a new file is uploaded to OneDrive or a new blob is added to Blob storage.

> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=214)** Actions are the steps that the workflow takes in response to the trigger.

>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=224)** We could add a new document to Cosmos DB or translate text to a specific language using Microsoft Translator.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=231)** Each operation is populated with data.
>
> **[3:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=233)** This data can be used by the actions in the Logic app.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=237)** This is how we pass information from one action to another.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=240)** For example, in the Outlook connector, we can get the contact and the email body of an email.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=246)** Then later in the workflow, we can use that information to create a Slack message or create a Google Calendar event.
>
> **[4:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/building-powerful-workflows-with-logic-apps?u=76281980&t=252)** Let's try and clarify with the diagram.

### 6. Azure Storage

#### A quick tour of Azure Storage
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Presenter] Azure has a variety of services that are optimized for storing data in the cloud.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=4)** Data comes in many forms and formats, so the services cater to these various shapes.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=10)** Databases are one type of storage.
>

>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=17)** That's the topic for another chapter.

>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=23)** There are services for file storage and file backup.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=26)** There are others for long-term archival data.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=29)** The Azure Storage account is the container for your data.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=32)** You must have at least one Storage account.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=34)** Within the Storage account, you can store various types of data, blob, file, queue, table, and disk.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=41)** You'll configure one or more of these types within the Storage account.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=45)** Each Storage service is optimized for a specific usage scenario.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=49)** Blob storage provides some client libraries and a REST interface that allow unstructured data to be stored and accessed at a massive scale.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=56)** It is perfect for storing audio and video files, and you can stream those as requested.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=61)** The data isn't structured.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=62)** There's no need to define a schema in Blob Storage.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=65)** Files can be massive in size.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=68)** Use when the app needs streaming or random access.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=71)** Data stored in the cloud grows at an exponential pace.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=74)** To manage costs for your expanding data storage needs, it's helpful to organize your data based on attributes like frequency of access and planned retention periods to optimize costs.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=85)** Azure Storage offers different access tiers, which allows you to store your data in the most cost effective manner.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=92)** The available access tiers include Hot, which is optimized for storing data that is accessed frequently, Cool, which is optimized for storing data that is infrequently accessed and stored for at least 30 days, Archive is optimized for storing data that is rarely accessed and is stored for at least 180 days.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=110)** Azure Files storage can be used to completely replace or supplement traditional on-premises file servers.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=116)** One thing that distinguishes Azure Files from files on a corporate file share is that you can access the files from anywhere in the world using a URL that points to the file.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=125)** The service also includes adding a shared access signature or an SAS token to a file.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=131)** With this feature, a user can allow access to a private asset for a specific amount of time.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=136)** Popular operating systems like Windows, Mac OS, and Linux can directly mount Azure file shares wherever they are in the world.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=144)** A good use for this is when you want to lift and shift an application to the cloud which already uses the native file system APIs to share data between it and other applications running in Azure.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=153)** Azure Queue Storage is a service for storing and retrieving messages.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=157)** Services create messages and add to the queue.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=160)** where they stay in a secure location until a consuming service removes the message for further processing.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=166)** A single queue message can be up to 64 KB in size, and a queue can contain millions of messages.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=172)** Now let's talk about Disk Storage.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=174)** These are disks for virtual machines.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=176)** Just like any other computer, virtual machines in Azure use disks as a place to store their operating system, applications, and data.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=183)** Azure Disk Storage is optimized for high IO operations.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=186)** You can put virtual HD images on the disk so that if you have a current drive configuration, you can move it to Azure.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=194)** You can also share one disk between multiple virtual machines.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=198)** This is useful when you want to store data that is not required to be accessed from outside the virtual machine to which the disc is attached.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=205)** You choose the level of hardware.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=206)** You can have standard HDD drives, and you can do standard or premium SSDs.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=211)** The better the hardware, the more it costs.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=213)** Azure Table Storage is a service that stores non-relational structured data, also known as No-SQL data, in the cloud.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=221)** It provides a key-value attribute store with a schemeless design.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=224)** While Azure Table Storage is still available, it is recommended to use the Azure Cosmos DB implementation instead.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=231)** Check out my Cosmos DB Table API course for more details.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=236)** All of these services share common features.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=239)** Like data encryption, data at rest refers to inactive data which is stored physically in any digital form.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=245)** That could be a database, a data warehouse, and Azure Storage.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=249)** Because the data is always encrypted, the data is safe because it is never stored in clear format.
>
> **[4:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=255)** All access to the storage goes through the Azure authentication and authorization pipeline, so you have full control over who has access to the data.
>
> **[4:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=263)** By default, everything you store in Azure Storage is replicated multiple times within the main regional data center.
>
> **[4:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=269)** These copies are placed on separate machines for safekeeping, plus you can configure Azure to replicate to a secondary data center.
>
> **[4:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=276)** So that's a brief look at Azure Storage.
>
> **[4:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=279)** There are other services which I didn't cover, like Azure Backup, a simple, secure, and cost effective solution to backup data and recover it from the Microsoft Azure Cloud.
>
> **[4:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=288)** Then there is Azure Data Lake Storage.
>
> **[4:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-storage?u=76281980&t=290)** Data lakes are a centralized repository that allow you to store all your structured and unstructured data in one place, then run data analytics across the lake.

#### Store any kind of object in blob storage
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Let's explore Azure Blob storage, one of the options for putting data in a storage account.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=5)** It's designed to store unstructured files; that's just a way of saying that we can store any type of file There is no structure required for the file type.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=12)** A BLOB, which is binary large object, consists of binary data stored as a single item.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=17)** An MP3 file is a BLOB, so is a PDF file.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=21)** To use Azure storage, start by creating a storage account.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=23)** This is the container for all of your storage items.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=27)** Name your storage account with a unique name.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=29)** No two storage accounts can have the same name on Azure.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=32)** I've called mine BigPicture.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=34)** That name becomes part of the URL that is used to access to stored data.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=37)** Every object that you store in Azure storage has an address and includes this unique account name.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=42)** So you can find it at BigPicture; that's my chosen name, .blob.core.[windows.net](https://windows.net).
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=49)** Next, we configure the storage services.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=51)** Here I'm setting up a BLOB storage within my storage account.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=54)** Storage accounts are containers for all storage types, so we can add a queue and we can add all the other storage types like disk, table, and file.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=62)** When working with BLOBs, we can also use a container.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=64)** A container organizes a set of BLOBs similar to a directory in a file system.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=70)** A storage account can include an unlimited number of containers, and a container can store an unlimited number of BLOBs.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=76)** When adding a BLOB, we put it into the container.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=78)** Here I have got two containers, one called Images, and the other called Videos.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=82)** Of course, the BLOBs will have names.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=84)** The name becomes part of the URL, so I've got a logo.png file in my Images container, and I've got an intro.avi file in my videos container.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=93)** So if I wanted to access the logo file, I would go to bigpicture.blob.core.[windows.net/images](https://windows.net/images).
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=103)** That gets me to the container, and then I specify the logo.png.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=107)** Here's some use cases: serving images directly to a browser, streaming video and audio, and creating and logging information into a log file.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=116)** These are just a few of the use cases; I'm sure you can think of others.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/store-any-kind-of-object-in-blob-storage?u=76281980&t=120)** After all, it's just a convenient way of storing files in the cloud.

### 7. Azure Databases

#### A quick tour of Azure databases
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=36)** It's ideal for modern cloud native applications due to its fast provisioning, scalability, and elasticity on the database capacity.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=44)** Azure SQL database is perfect when you need to store relational database in a transactional system with heavy duty querying capabilities.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=51)** Azure SQL Database is the fully managed cloud equivalent of the on-premises SQL Server product that has been around for decades.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=58)** It is a schema-based system where the structure of your data is encoded in the database plan, you store data in tables with rows and columns.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=67)** It supports familiar SQL Server features, like stored procedures, user defined functions, and all of the T-SQL language spec.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=74)** Azure SQL Database is a very mature and advanced database.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=77)** Azure SQL Database Hyperscale is a service tier in Azure SQL Database.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=82)** I like to think of it as an extension of the standard Azure SQL Database.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=87)** It provides additional features like highly scalable storage and compute performance.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=92)** It's designed to handle large databases with ease, supporting up to 100 terabyte of data.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=97)** Key features include rapid scaling of computer resources, high transaction log throughput, and fast database backups and restores.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=106)** It's ideal for businesses that need to scale quickly without compromising on performance.
>

>

> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=147)** It could well become the dominant system in the Azure Cloud database ecosystem.
>

>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=159)** That means if you have non-relational or NoSQL data, this is a good candidate for storage.

>

>

>

>
> **[5:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=317)** With it, you can query both relational and non-relational data using the familiar SQL language.
>
> **[5:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=323)** This can be done using serverless on demand queries for data exploration and ad hoc analysis.
>
> **[5:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=328)** It deeply integrates with Power BI, providing a valuable tool for business users.
>
> **[5:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=333)** Additionally, data scientists find it an invaluable resource for coding statistical models with Azure Machine Learning.
>
> **[5:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=339)** A data lake is like a giant storage pool where you can keep all your data in its original raw format.
>
> **[5:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=346)** Azure's Data Lake is specifically designed for big data, capable of handling everything from terabytes to petabytes of data from various sources, whether it's structured, semi-structured, or unstructured data.
>
> **[5:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=358)** Unlike traditional data warehouses, it stores data as is without transforming it during ingestion, which is great for big data environments where you don't yet know what insights you'll find.
>
> **[6:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=371)** Users can explore and query this data, making it perfect for analytics, reporting, and machine learning.
>
> **[6:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=376)** It's built on Azure Blob Storage.
>
> **[6:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=378)** It adds interesting features like file system semantics, file level security, and scalability.
>
> **[6:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=385)** So that's a brief look at the various database services available in Azure.
>
> **[6:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/a-quick-tour-of-azure-databases?u=76281980&t=389)** There are many attractive options.

#### Explore Cosmos DB, the multimodel, no-SQL database
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980)

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The latest database advance from Microsoft is Azure Cosmos DB.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=4)** It is a versatile, globally-distributed database service.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=8)** It's designed to effortlessly scale and perform for today's modern applications.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=14)** Think of it as your all-in-one NoSQL and vector database that delivers lightning-fast, single-digit millisecond response times and instant scalability to handle loads of data and traffic.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=26)** We've seen the steady rise of non-relational database systems during the internet and machine learning era.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=32)** While relational databases still are viable, non-relational, also known as NoSQL, databases were created to solve important data challenges that relational databases couldn't handle.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=43)** The major challenge in modern data collection is how to deal with big data, data that is too big for traditional relational systems to handle.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=51)** Research shows that the trouble arises in three areas: volume, velocity, and variety, also known as the three Vs.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=60)** Volume refers to the amount of information stored in our systems.

>

>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=76)** Volume at enormous size poses problems in many areas.

>

>
