>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=166)** One of the coolest things about Azure Cosmos DB is its multi-model magic.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=170)** Whether you're working with documents, key-value pairs, graphs, or column-family data, it's got you covered.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=176)** This flexibility means you can pick the data model that fits your app perfectly without being stuck in one mold.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=183)** Azure's Cosmos DB global distribution is another game-changer.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=186)** It lets you replicate data across any of Azure's global regions, ensuring your users get speedy, reliable access no matter where they are.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=194)** And the best part: this replication happens automatically, so you don't have to lift a finger.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=200)** Azure Cosmos DB effortlessly manages scaling operations, offering boundless storage scalability.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=206)** It achieves this through proactive monitoring of data expansion and dynamically adjusts capacity via server-side partitioning.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=214)** Similarly, for data throughput, you determine the desired performance metrics, and Cosmos DB ensures consistent delivery by automatically provisioning data replicas to meet your specific performance targets.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=226)** And this reduces latency.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=228)** The closer your data is to your users, the faster your system can work with that data.
>
> **[3:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=233)** A big plus with Azure Cosmos DB is its top-notch indexing strategy.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=237)** Every property and every item is indexed by default, allowing you to run super fast queries without worrying about schema or index management.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=246)** Plus, you can tweak the indexing policies to suit your needs, giving you the perfect blend of simplicity and power.
>
> **[4:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=252)** You have control over index update models.
>
> **[4:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=255)** Lazy updates are performed asynchronously, utilizing a background process to reduce indexing cost.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=262)** On the other hand, consistent updates are executed in real time, ensuring immediate data availability, but at a higher cost.
>
> **[4:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=269)** Azure Cosmos DB plays nicely with other Azure services, like Azure Functions and Azure AI.
>
> **[4:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=275)** This makes interacting with the database a breeze.
>
> **[4:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=278)** With its robust features and seamless integration with the Azure ecosystem, this database is a fantastic choice for building scalable, high-performance applications.
>
> **[4:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=287)** Cosmos DB uses an interesting data model called atom-record-sequence, or ARS, which makes it easy to convert different data types into a unified format.
>
> **[4:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=297)** Think of atoms as basic types, like strings or numbers, records as structured data, and sequences as arrays of atoms, records, or other sequences.
>
> **[5:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=306)** This ARS model is key to Cosmos DB's ability to handle multiple data models without slowing down.
>
> **[5:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=313)** When you want to work with data in Cosmos DB, you can choose from several APIs, each designed for a specific type of data.
>
> **[5:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=320)** When you need to access the data, you can choose from any of the four support APIs.
>
> **[5:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=325)** Each API works with the underlying ARS data model, but presents the data in the specific style of the chosen API.
>
> **[5:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=332)** For example, let's assume you need to work with JSON Documents.
>
> **[5:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=335)** In that case, you'd use the SQL API.
>
> **[5:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=339)** It lets you work with document data using a familiar SQL syntax that's been extended to support JSON.
>
> **[5:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=345)** This API is built right into Cosmos DB and gives you full control over the interface, service, and SDK client libraries.
>
> **[5:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=353)** It's the best option for a seamless experience.
>
> **[5:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=356)** For graph data, go for the Gremlin API, which is based on a Apache TinkerPop, a graph computing framework.
>
> **[6:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=363)** It offers a powerful and expressive language for querying and manipulating graph data.
>
> **[6:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=368)** This API is perfect for scenarios involve complex relationships and interconnected data points.
>
> **[6:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=373)** For column-family data, use the Cassandra API.
>
> **[6:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=377)** It lets you interact with data using the Cassandra Query Language.
>
> **[6:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=381)** It's designed for applications built for Apache Cassandra and is compatible with Cassandra-based tools and client drivers.
>
> **[6:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=388)** Finally, we have table data via the Table API.
>
> **[6:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=392)** Table data is helpful for applications that need a flexible, schemaless storage system for structured and NoSQL data.
>
> **[6:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=399)** This API is especially useful for those moving from the depreciated Azure Table Storage.
>
> **[6:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=404)** The Table API is perfect for large-scale applications that need a wide column store, that can easily scale.
>
> **[6:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=410)** It supports a variety of SDKs, including .NET, Java, Python, Node.js, and Go, making it accessible to many developers.
>
> **[6:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=419)** Each of these APIs is designed to make the most of Cosmos DB core features, like global distribution, elastic scaling of storage and throughput and low latency.
>
> **[7:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=428)** This fully-managed platform can handle both transactional and analytical workloads at any scale.
>
> **[7:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=434)** So whether you're working with documents or graphs or column-family data or even table data, Cosmos DB has a diverse API selection that ensures you can use the tools and skills you already have to model and query your data effectively.
>
> **[7:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=449)** This database is an interesting service that offers a flexible way to store data at massive scale across global regions.
>
> **[7:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=455)** You can start small in a single region, and with just a few clicks, expand your data to other regions.
>
> **[7:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-cosmos-db-the-multimodel-no-sql-database?u=76281980&t=461)** It is known for its speed and data insertion and retrieval thanks to its automatic indexing of non-relational data, which ensures quick queries.

### 8. Infrastructure

#### Protect access to services with Microsoft Entra ID
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Identity and access management is a critical component for modern organizations providing a structured approach to managing digital identities and ensuring secure access to resources.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=10)** In this video, I want to look at why it's indispensable for your Azure subscription.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=14)** One of the primary benefits is its ability to enhance security and mitigate various risks.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=20)** These systems ensure that only authorized users can access specific resources for legitimate reasons while blocking unauthorized access and activities.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=29)** This is crucial because user login credentials are often a significant factor in data breaches.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=34)** By implementing robust identity and access management policies, organizations can protect sensitive data and reduce the likelihood of security incidents.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=43)** Having a good identity and access management system helps organizations meet regulatory requirements by ensuring proper data handling and access controls.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=53)** They provide a framework for monitoring and reporting access to sensitive information, helping organizations demonstrate compliance with regulations such as GDPR, HIPAA and others.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=63)** The rise of remote work and cloud computing has heightened the importance of these types of solutions.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=68)** These systems effectively manage remote employees access to company resources through the cloud, ensuring secure and efficient operations.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=75)** Microsoft Active Directory and Microsoft Entra ID are both identity access management services, but they serve different purposes and offer different capabilities.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=85)** Entra ID is the new name for Azure Active Directory.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=89)** Microsoft Entra ID is Microsoft's cloud-based identity and access management service.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=95)** It provides the authentication and authorization services so that your resources are available to your employees and kept safe from the outside world.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=102)** It plays a crucial role in enhancing cloud security and providing a single point of control over who has access to what in your organization.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=111)** We'll need to have an authentication and authorization system in place.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=114)** That's a given for any cloud service.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=116)** Using Entra ID is the easiest way to make that happen in Azure.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=120)** It will seem familiar to anyone comfortable with using Windows Active directory, but know that it is a cloud optimized version.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=126)** If you already have an on-premises active directory, it can be extended to the cloud using the directory integration capabilities of Entra ID.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=134)** Entra ID can also be your organization's only directory service.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=138)** This is especially true for many startups today who rely on Microsoft 365 or other SaaS applications for their software needs.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=147)** They don't need to have an on-premises active directory as Entra ID manages their users' identity and access to SaaS applications.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=155)** It's all done online.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=156)** Like all things in Azure, we can manage Entra ID through the portal.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=159)** Along the left side, we can see choices for managing users and groups, setting up roles and administrators, and even a section on working with custom domains.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=168)** We can also manage our Entra ID through the PowerShell command line.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=171)** Here we are preparing to add a new user to the directory.

> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=175)** With Entra ID, you are able to offer your employees a single sign-on capability even to services outside of your organization.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=182)** Entra ID is very scalable and provides high availability to its services.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=186)** Plus, like all cloud infrastructure, your organization doesn't have to maintain related infrastructure or worry about disaster recovery.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=194)** All development related to identity management in your organization gets easier since Entra ID utilizes standardized REST and ODATA protocols.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=203)** If required, you can easily use identity providers from Google or Facebook and others, which is useful for extranet situations.

> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=211)** To summarize, you automatically get Entra ID with your Azure subscription.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=215)** It's already available and configured with a few identities to get you started.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/protect-access-to-services-with-microsoft-entra-id?u=76281980&t=219)** With little effort, you can expand to manage your entire organization.

#### Explore the Azure networking components
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Building a network of interconnected systems is a lot like putting together a Lego creation, but with hardwares and wires, not plastic blocks.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=7)** With Azure, you can build out your network system from the web tool or the command line, and Microsoft creates the system for you.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=14)** This is the essence of Infrastructure-as-a-Service.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=16)** Let's look at the components that are available for your virtual network.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=20)** This shows the network components available in the Azure portal.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=23)** There are a lot of choices.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=25)** Essentially, if you can add a type of hardware component to your data center, you can add it to Azure networking.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=31)** Microsoft has a number of partners that also offer networking devices that can plug into your virtual network.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=36)** These are available alongside the other Azure network components, which makes them just as easy to add as any other component.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=42)** The advantage here is especially important if you are doing a lift and shift to the cloud, and you have third party hardware in your data center.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=49)** The backbone of Azure networking is the Azure Virtual Network, also called the VNET.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=54)** Think of the Azure VNET as a representation of your own network in the cloud.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=58)** It is a logical isolation of the Azure Cloud dedicated to your subscription.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=63)** Inside the VNET resides the other networking components.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=66)** Remember, if you are building VNETs, you are doing infrastructure as a service, so you'll need to create all the other parts of your infrastructure.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=72)** So a VNET becomes a central hub used to group any resources that need to be accessible on our Azure infrastructure, like our virtual machines, or storage accounts, or databases, they can all reside inside the virtual network.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=83)** Let's look at some popular networking components.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=87)** ExpressRoute is a Microsoft Azure service that lets you create private connections between Microsoft data centers and infrastructure that is on your premises or in a co-location facility.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=97)** ExpressRoute connections do not go over the public internet.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=100)** Instead, they go through telecom fiber connections.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=103)** They enable higher security, reliability, and speeds with lower latencies than typical connections over the internet.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=110)** A VPN gateway is a specific type of virtual network gateway that is used to ascend encrypted traffic between an Azure virtual network, and an on-premise location over the public internet.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=121)** You can also use a VPN gateway to send encrypted traffic between Azure virtual networks over the Microsoft network.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=127)** Load balancing refers to efficiently distributing network traffic across a group of servers, also known as a server farm or a server pool.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=136)** Azure Load Balancer provides inbound and outbound scenarios, provides low latency and high throughput, and scales up to millions of flows for all TCP and UDP applications.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=146)** Load balancer distributes new inbound flows that arrive on the load balancer's front end to the backend pool instances according to a set of rules and health probes.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=156)** Additionally, a public load balancer can provide outbound connections for virtual machines inside your virtual network by translating their private IP addresses to public IP addresses.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=167)** You can set up your own custom IP addresses.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=170)** You can assign IP addresses to Azure resources to communicate with other Azure resources with your on-premises network and the internet.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=178)** There are two types of IP addresses you can use in Azure: public and private.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=182)** Public IP addresses are used for communication with the internet, including Azure Public facing services.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=188)** Private IP addresses are used for communication within the Azure VNET and your on-premises network when you use a VPN gateway, or ExpressRoute circuit to extend your network to Azure.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=199)** In computing, a firewall is a network security system that monitors and controls incoming and outgoing network traffic based on predetermined security rules.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=208)** A firewall typically establishes a barrier between a trusted internal network and untrusted external networks such as the internet.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=216)** Azure Firewall is a managed cloud-based network security service that protects your Azure VNET resources.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=221)** To conclude, Azure provides an abundance of networking tools for your cloud.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=226)** We've looked at some of the major elements.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/explore-the-azure-networking-components?u=76281980&t=228)** There is still more to explore like DNS zones and CDN providers.

> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/build-out-your-system-with-virtual-machines?u=76281980&t=122)** After the deployment is completed, you use remote desktop to connect to the virtual machine and manage it like any other server.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/build-out-your-system-with-virtual-machines?u=76281980&t=129)** Though I didn't show it in the earlier screenshots, you can specify credentials like username and password during the provisioning, or better yet, use Entra ID and work with your existing admin accounts.

### 9. DevOps

#### Simplify app deployment with containers
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] DevOps is a set of cultural practices related to software development.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980&t=4)** It emphasizes collaboration between all parts of the IT organization and the continuous delivery of software.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980&t=9)** Containers are a type of technology that makes it easier to host applications inside portable deployable environments.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980&t=16)** Containers make it possible to isolate applications into small, lightweight execution environments that share the operating system kernel.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980&t=23)** The most popular container by far is Docker.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980&t=27)** Microsoft Azure has full support for Docker.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980&t=29)** If you use the Azure app service for your web app or web API, you can either deploy your app directly to the app service or place the app within a Docker container and deploy the container instead.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980&t=40)** Containers offer several key benefits that help enable DevOps workflow.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980&t=44)** When you write, test and deploy your application inside containers, the environment does not change as it moves through development, testing, and production environments.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980&t=53)** This makes collaboration between different teams like the developers, testers and admins easier because they are all working with the same containerized environment.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980&t=61)** Continuously delivering software requires rolling out application updates on a constant efficient basis.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980&t=67)** Containers help ease the anxiety around the deployment process because they make it easy to apply updates.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980&t=73)** Developers love containers.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980&t=75)** Collaborating on code with coworkers is better because all of the dependencies run in the containers, eliminating the works on my machine problems, plus it helps automate the repetitive tasks of setting up and configuring development environments.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980&t=88)** For operations, they can use Docker to manage apps side by side and isolated containers to get better compute density.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980&t=96)** Plus, it definitely makes it easier to streamline software delivery to the testing and production servers.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980&t=101)** Using Docker and Azure App Service is simple.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980&t=104)** Here's a sample of how to do this from Visual Studio.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980&t=107)** When creating a new project, simply check the enabled Docker support checkbox.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980&t=111)** Visual Studio does the work of creating the Docker container.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/simplify-app-deployment-with-containers?u=76281980&t=114)** Later when you deploy the application, it is pushed to the app service within the container.

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/github-and-azure?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] Judging from the number of questions I get, there is some confusion about how GitHub fits into the Azure ecosystem.

> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/github-and-azure?u=76281980&t=25)** Since it is a distributed system, every team member has a copy of the repository on their local computer.
>

#### Azure deployment environments: Streamline cloud infrastructure management
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] Earlier in this chapter, we looked at containers and how they are essential in continuous integration and continuous deployment pipelines.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=8)** Microsoft created the Azure Deployment Environments to help Azure customers easily configure their deployment systems.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=15)** To review, Docker containers ensure consistency across development, testing, and production environments.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=21)** Developers can confidently reproduce the same environment, eliminating discrepancies between local setups and deployment.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=28)** Docker images can be rapidly built, shipped, and deployed.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=32)** The lightweight nature of containers allows for quick distribution.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=35)** Containers isolate applications and their dependencies.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=39)** Each container runs independently, preventing conflicts with other apps or system libraries.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=44)** Consistent environments across development, testing, and production stages lead to more reliable deployments.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=50)** We know that containers are an effective solution for our CI/CD pipeline.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=54)** That's great, but there are additional considerations such as the best way to set up and configure them.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=60)** For a simple project, one container might suffice for development testing and deployment.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=64)** However, this is not the case for enterprise clients and other complex application development groups.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=70)** In such scenarios, dozens of specialized configurations might be necessary, and the IT team needs to ensure that the containers in the entire pipeline comply with security and other company policies.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=83)** Azure Deployment Environments aims to help ease this burden.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=86)** They empower development teams to quickly and easily spin up app infrastructure with project-based templates that establish consistency and best practices while maximizing security.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=98)** This on-demand access to secure environments accelerates the stages of software development in a compliant and a cost-efficient way.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=105)** A deployment environment is a collection of Azure infrastructure resources defined in a template called an environment definition.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=113)** Developers can deploy these templates in accessible subscriptions and build their applications on the provided infrastructure.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=120)** For example, a deployment environment can include a web app, database, and a storage account, allowing your web developer to start coding the web app without concern for the underlying infrastructure.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=131)** This diagram from the Azure documentation site provides an overview of the Azure Deployment Environments.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=137)** Platform engineers set up infrastructure templates and manage subscriptions, identity, and permissions.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=143)** Developers use these templates to create environments for building and deploying applications.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-deployment-environments-streamline-cloud-infrastructure-management?u=76281980&t=147)** These environments support various scenarios such as on-demand environments, testing sandboxes, and CI/CD pipelines.

> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=83)** Machine learning is important, because it allows software to learn and improve from data.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=87)** This can lead to more accurate and efficient decision making.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=91)** By analyzing patterns and trends and data, machine learning algorithms can identify insights and make predictions faster than humans.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=98)** For example, say we want to classify music into categories like hip hop, rock, or dubstep.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=105)** Rather than establishing categorization rules, developers input thousands of examples of each music genre into the machine learning algorithm.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=113)** The algorithm then identifies patterns within the music and utilizes these characteristics to recognize and catalog other songs.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=120)** Machine learning serves as the fundamental building block of Azure AI, providing the backbone upon which many of its key features and capabilities are built in.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=129)** The machine learning algorithms are used to analyze data and identify patterns or relationships in that data.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=135)** An AI algorithm is a set of instructions or rules that a computer program follows to perform a specific task.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=142)** It is a step-by-step process that takes input data and produces output data based on a set of rules.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=148)** This collection of algorithms is used to train the AI model.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=151)** The process of training a machine learning model involves feeding it large amounts of data and allowing it to learn from that data over time.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=160)** The algorithm used to train the model will adjust the model's parameters based on the data that it receives.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=166)** It does this in order to improve its accuracy and performance.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=169)** Once the model has been trained, it can be used to make predictions or decisions based on new data that it encounters.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=175)** Azure offers a variety of tools and services that allow developers to build, train, and deploy custom machine learning models.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=183)** One way to create custom models in Azure is to use the Azure machine learning studio.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=188)** This is a web-based integrated development environment for building machine learning models.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=193)** With Azure machine learning studio, developers can drag and drop modules to create a machine learning workflow and then use the platform to train and deploy their models.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=202)** Another option is to use the Azure machine learning service in the Azure portal.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=207)** This is more time consuming for developers and data scientists, but it provides more customization.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=211)** For the last few years, Microsoft has grouped the AI services into categories like cognitive services and applied AI services.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=219)** Microsoft has officially dropped these category names.
>
> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=222)** The features are still available, just renamed Azure AI services.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=226)** You don't need to create your own models, however.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=228)** That's because Azure offers a variety of pre-built machine learning models and services, which provide developers with ready to use APIs for tests like image recognition.
>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=238)** With tools like this, Azure can analyze the content of your images or videos and identify specific content.
>
> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=244)** Azure AI services is a suite of prebuilt machine learning models and APIs.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=249)** These services provide a range of capabilities including vision, speech, language, and decision making.
>
> **[4:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=255)** Another subcategory of AI is large language models or LLMs.
>
> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=260)** They are a specific type of machine learning model that is specifically designed to process and understand natural language.
>
> **[4:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=266)** While other machine learning models may be designed to process structure data such as numerical or categorical data, large language models are designed to process unstructured data, such as text or speech.
>
> **[4:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=278)** This requires different techniques and algorithms for processing and analyzing the data.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=282)** LLMs are typically built using deep learning techniques such as neural networks and are trained on large amounts of text data to learn patterns and relationships in language.
>
> **[4:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=293)** Some of Azure services are based on large language models.
>
> **[4:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=296)** For example, the language understanding service sometimes called LUIS is based on a large language model that has been trained on a vast amount of text data to understand natural language queries and commands.
>
> **[5:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=308)** LUIS allows developers to build natural language processing capabilities into their application, enabling users to interact with the application using conversational language.
>
> **[5:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=318)** Similarly, the text analytics service is based on large language models that have been trained on a vast amount of text data to identify sentiment, key phrases and other insights in the text.
>
> **[5:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=331)** This service can be used to analyze customer feedback, social media posts, and other text data to gain insights into customer behavior and preferences.
>
> **[5:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=340)** One of the most popular pre-trained LLMs is offered by OpenAI, an artificial intelligence research laboratory.
>
> **[5:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=346)** ChatGPT is a pre-trained language model for conversational AI based on the generative pre-trained transformer architecture.
>
> **[5:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=354)** That's where you get the abbreviation GPT.
>
> **[5:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=357)** GPT is a type of neural network.
>
> **[5:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=359)** ChatGPT is designed to generate human-like responses to natural language queries and commands, and can be fine tuned for specific use cases.
>
> **[6:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=368)** Microsoft is a significant partner with OpenAI, which means that we can use OpenAI models and services from Azure.
>
> **[6:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=375)** AI models can be paired with generation tools, so the vast amount of information gathered via machine learning can be used to create new content.
>
> **[6:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=383)** Because of this, machine learning is having a significant impact on the creative world.
>
> **[6:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=387)** For example, machine learning algorithms can be used to generate music, art, and even literature by analyzing patterns and styles in existing works and creating new ones based on that analysis.
>
> **[6:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=399)** One popular generative tool is DALL-E, a neural network based image generation system developed by OpenAI.
>
> **[6:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=406)** It can generate high quality images from textual descriptions.
>
> **[6:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=409)** The system is trained on a massive data set of images and text and uses a combination of deep learning techniques to generate images that match the given textual descriptions.
>
> **[6:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=419)** Because of the Microsoft partnership with OpenAI, we can use DALL-E in our applications.
>
> **[7:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=423)** Finally, let's look at the Internet of Things.
>
> **[7:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=426)** It refers to a group of connected or network set of physical devices, vehicles, home appliances, and other items that are embedded with sensors, software, and connectivity.
>
> **[7:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=436)** IoT is rapidly expanding with billions of devices already connected to the internet and many more expected to come online in the coming years.
>
> **[7:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=445)** This vast network of connected devices has the potential to transform industries ranging from healthcare and manufacturing to transportation and agriculture.
>
> **[7:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=454)** AI is poised to play a crucial role in unlocking the full potential of IoT.
>
> **[7:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=459)** By applying machine learning algorithms to the massive amount of data generated by IoT devices, we can gain deeper insights into the patterns and trends, identifying anomalies and outliers, and make more accurate predictions.
>
> **[7:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-azure-ai-family?u=76281980&t=472)** Azure has a comprehensive set of AI services, which include many machine learning tools.
