#### Messaging with event grid, event hub, or service bus
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Azure offers multiple communication options for messaging between services.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=5)** This is often necessary for integration of separate distributed services.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=8)** These options ensure efficient and reliable data exchange across different components in an application.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=13)** Azure's flexibility allows developers to select the most suitable messaging service based on specific requirements.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=19)** Here's a look at the available messaging components.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=22)** Event Grid simplifies building event driven architectures with its fully managed event routing service using a published subscribed model.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=30)** Event Hubs is a big data streaming platform that can handle millions of events per second.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=36)** The Service Bus provides enterprise-level messaging and it also offers published subscribed capabilities for one-to-many messaging.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=43)** Azure Relay securely bridges on-premises networks to the cloud for bidirectional point to point communication.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=51)** Together, these tools offer a comprehensive, scalable and secure messaging infrastructure in Azure.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=57)** In this video, we'll look at the first three.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=59)** In message systems, there is a sender and a receiver.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=63)** It is common for these messages to be sent asynchronously, which avoids coupling between the sender and receiver.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=70)** In some scenarios, the sender requires the receiver to perform an action and acknowledge the success or failure of the action, thus sending a message back to the sender.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=79)** Software architects break down this general principle of sender and receiver into named patterns.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=85)** You'll hear this pattern described as publisher subscriber, or often called pub sub, and producer consumer.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=92)** Let's use YouTube as an analogy.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=94)** The publisher subscriber model can be compared to a YouTube channel.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=98)** When a channel, the publisher, uploads a new video, all of its subscribers are notified and have access to the video.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=105)** Just like subscribers to a YouTube channel all receive the same content, subscribers in a pub sub model all receive the same messages.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=113)** Consider the producer consumer model as akin to a YouTube content creator producer, and their video editor, the consumer.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=120)** The content creator produces raw video footage, the messages, and expects the video editor to edit and enhance it, in this case, performing some action.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=130)** Each piece of footage is assigned to a specific editor, distributing the workload among multiple editors.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=136)** This way, each video is processed individually, like how each message in a producer consumer model is consumed by a specific consumer.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=144)** These patterns are more complex than my brief explanation suggests, but this simplified version should be sufficient for now.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=151)** An important refinement to this process is to use a message broker, which sits between the producer and consumer.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=157)** Messages are sent to the broker, and the broker forwards them to the consumer.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=161)** Brokers provide additional benefits, such as prioritizing messages to ensure higher priority messages are sent first.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=168)** They also enhance reliability.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=171)** If the consumer has a connection problem, the message remains in the broker until the connection is reestablished.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=177)** Azure Service Bus is the service for Azure.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=180)** Azure events and Azure commands are two different types of messages used in Azure messaging services.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=186)** Here's how they differ.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=188)** The difference between the two is defined by what the publisher wants the consumer to do with the message.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=193)** With a command, that producer expects the consumer to perform an action.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=197)** With an event, the publisher sends information that something has happened.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=201)** In Azure, if you want a publisher to issue a command, you will typically use Azure Service Bus.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=206)** You can issue events using both Azure Event Grid and Azure Event Hubs, but they serve different purposes.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=212)** Event Grid is designed for reactive event-driven architectures, allowing you to publish and route events to various handlers.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=219)** It is ideal for scenarios where you need to react to changes in state or updates in real time.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=225)** Event Hubs, on the other hand, is optimized for high throughput event ingestion and processing, suitable for streaming large amounts of data from various sources, such as telemetry and logs.
>
> **[3:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=235)** A command is a high-value message and must be delivered at least once.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=239)** If a command is lost, the entire business transaction might fail.
>
> **[4:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=243)** Also, a command shouldn't be processed more than once.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=246)** As to event messages, the publisher sends out the event without needing to know which consumers will receive it.
>
> **[4:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=252)** Consumers that are interested in the event can subscribe to it, listen for occurrences, and take actions based on their needs.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=259)** An event can have multiple subscribers or none at all, and different subscribers can react to the same event with distinct actions without being aware of each other.
>
> **[4:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=268)** Events largely fall into two big categories.
>
> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=271)** Discreet events represent specific actions carried out by the publishing application, such as a user logging in or an order being shipped, and are often used to trigger actions in other system parts.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=282)** Series events provide continuous data streams, like telemetry or logging.
>
> **[4:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=288)** These are used in real time processing, such as temperature sensor publishing.
>
> **[4:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=291)** In Azure, use Service Bus for transactional workflows or command messages.
>
> **[4:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=296)** In the transactional scenario, the message will carry information that delegates the handling of specific steps in a workflow or processing chain to different roles within a system.
>
> **[5:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=306)** These messages, such as purchase orders or monetary account transfer records, may hold significant value.
>
> **[5:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=312)** If such a message were lost, it could be challenging to recover.
>
> **[5:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=316)** These messages might need to be transferred by certain deadlines, at specific times, and in a particular order.
>
> **[5:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=323)** Additionally, messages can include commands to perform specific actions.
>
> **[5:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=327)** The expectation is the consumer will perform the action.
>
> **[5:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=330)** The producer may also expect the receivers to report back the outcome, providing a path for these reports to be sent back.
>
> **[5:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=337)** Messages in this scenario are good for coordinating steps in a workflow.
>
> **[5:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=341)** For example, the producer could message the first step consumer and wait for a success message.
>
> **[5:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=346)** Then the producer could send a message to the second step consumer.
>
> **[5:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=349)** Messages are also useful for transactions where there must be consistency, like transferring money between accounts.
>
> **[5:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=355)** The transaction must complete safely rollback if failed.
>
> **[5:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=358)** Service Bus is a brokered messaging system.
>
> **[6:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=361)** It stores messages in a broker until the consuming party is ready to receive the messages.
>
> **[6:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=366)** The brokers are configurable, from simple queues, which send a command between one sender and one receiver, or choose the topic-based broker, which allows multiple consumers, and each consumer can filter the commands to the one it needs.
>
> **[6:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=381)** Service Bus supports enterprise- level features like transactions, ordering, duplicate detection, and instantaneous consistency.
>
> **[6:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=389)** It also ensures guaranteed delivery, which is useful if the application crashes.
>
> **[6:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=394)** In such cases, the message is redelivered when the application restarts.
>
> **[6:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=397)** This process is often referred to as at least once processing, meaning each message is processed to completion at least once.
>
> **[6:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=405)** Moving to another topic, events are also messages, but they typically do not convey a publisher's intent beyond providing information.
>
> **[6:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=413)** An event captures and conveys a fact, allowing the consumer to process it as they see fit without needing to fulfill any specific expectations of the publisher.
>
> **[7:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=422)** Repeating what I said earlier, there are two kinds of events.
>
> **[7:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=426)** Discreet events represent specific actions performed by the publishing application, such as the user logging in or an order being shipped.
>
> **[7:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=433)** These events are often used to trigger actions in other parts of the system.
>
> **[7:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=437)** In a series event system, an event is part of a continuous stream.
>
> **[7:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=441)** By itself, a single event from a stream is not very significant.
>
> **[7:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=445)** It is the stream as a whole that matters.
>
> **[7:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=447)** This is common in telemetry or logging scenarios, and is also useful for database history, as it allows the reconstruction of a database from the stream of actions.
>
> **[7:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=457)** Use Event Grid for discrete events and Azure Event Hubs For series events.
>
> **[7:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=462)** Azure Event Hubs is a telemetry ingestion service able to scale to collecting millions of events.
>
> **[7:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=468)** Telemetry is useful when you want to record information about usage and transmit the information elsewhere for processing and storage.
>
> **[7:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=475)** Let's say you have a solar farm in Arizona with 30,000 solar panels.
>
> **[7:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=479)** Each panel is outfitted with a sensor that collects information about the environment, the panel status, and diagnostics information.
>
> **[8:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=486)** Every five seconds, this data is transmitted to your data center.
>
> **[8:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=490)** That's 20 million messages per hour.
>
> **[8:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=493)** Event Hubs is a good choice for this scenario.
>
> **[8:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=495)** In fact, it can handle millions of events per second.
>
> **[8:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=498)** Use the Event Hubs service to collect data or events from any IoT device, from an app, whether that's web, or mobile, or backend service, or feeds like social networks.
>
> **[8:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=508)** The data is ingested into the hub where it is stored for later use.
>
> **[8:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=512)** Once you collect events within the event hub, you can analyze the data using any real time analytics system, such as the Azure Stream Analytics service.
>
> **[8:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=521)** Additionally, you can store or transform the hub data into any Azure data storage system.
>
> **[8:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=526)** Event Grid enables event driven reactive programming.
>
> **[8:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=529)** It uses a pub sub model.
>
> **[8:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=531)** Event Grid has built in support for events coming from Azure services, like Storage Blobs, and Resource Groups.
>
> **[8:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=538)** It also lends itself nicely to the serverless model of computing using Azure Cloud services, such as Azure Functions and Azure Logic Apps.
>
> **[9:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=546)** The system handles individual business logic activity events that are valuable on their own, not as part of a stream.
>
> **[9:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=553)** Since these events aren't closely related and don't need to be processed in batches, they are dispatched differently.
>
> **[9:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=559)** The model assumes that an application or platform service emits a large number of different events across various contexts.
>
> **[9:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=565)** A subscriber might only be interested in a specific event type or a specific context.
>
> **[9:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=571)** This leads to a filtered subscriber model where a consumer can choose exactly which subset of events they want to receive.
>
> **[9:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=578)** Event Grid can handle millions of messages, so it can scale to your needs.
>
> **[9:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=582)** There are many scenarios where your app might need all three services, so you can combine them as needed.
>
> **[9:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=587)** Also, there is integration among the services.
>
> **[9:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=590)** For example, Service Bus and Event Hubs can emit events into Event Grid.
>
> **[9:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=594)** So here's a scenario.
>
> **[9:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/messaging-with-event-grid-event-hub-or-service-bus?u=76281980&t=596)** If you have sporadic messages in Service Bus and your system goes idle while waiting for the next message, you can emit an event when the next message is added to the Service Bus queue.

#### Send mobile notifications with notification hubs

>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/send-mobile-notifications-with-notification-hubs?u=76281980&t=5)** Use it to quickly send millions of notifications to mobile devices.

>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/send-mobile-notifications-with-notification-hubs?u=76281980&t=73)** Tags let you segment customers based on activity, interest, location, or user preference.

> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/send-mobile-notifications-with-notification-hubs?u=76281980&t=80)** For example, your weather app could send a tornado warning only to devices in the impacted location.

>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/send-mobile-notifications-with-notification-hubs?u=76281980&t=97)** If your app covers multiple markets, then use the templates feature to give you a handy way to send localized push notifications so you're speaking to the customers in their languages.

> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/send-mobile-notifications-with-notification-hubs?u=76281980&t=111)** They eliminate the hassle of storing the localized sessions for each customer or creating hundreds of tags.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/send-mobile-notifications-with-notification-hubs?u=76281980&t=117)** The Notification Hub automatically handles the infrastructure necessary to scale your message to every active device with low latency.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/send-mobile-notifications-with-notification-hubs?u=76281980&t=124)** It also eliminates all the complexities associated with pushing notification on your own from your own app backend.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/send-mobile-notifications-with-notification-hubs?u=76281980&t=131)** It's multi-platform push notification infrastructure where it uses push-related coding and simplifies your backend.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/send-mobile-notifications-with-notification-hubs?u=76281980&t=138)** What needs to happen is each device is responsible for registering their platform notification systems with the hub.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/send-mobile-notifications-with-notification-hubs?u=76281980&t=145)** Then the Azure Service determines the best way to notify each device.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Analogies:** for example (3)
> **CLI Commands:** php (1), node (1)

> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/manage-iot-devices?u=76281980&t=147)** So here's a summary.

> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/manage-iot-devices?u=76281980&t=149)** IOT Central is software as a service, IOT Hub is platform as a service.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/manage-iot-devices?u=76281980&t=153)** With IOT Central, you're doing a turnkey system.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/manage-iot-devices?u=76281980&t=156)** It's immediately usable.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/manage-iot-devices?u=76281980&t=158)** Whereas with IOT Hub, you'll be building your own system.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/manage-iot-devices?u=76281980&t=161)** IOT Central is template based and is customizable.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/manage-iot-devices?u=76281980&t=164)** IOT Hub is more developer focused and both of these are built on the solid Azure core.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/manage-iot-devices?u=76281980&t=171)** Azure IOT Edge is a fully managed service built on Azure IOT hub.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/manage-iot-devices?u=76281980&t=175)** Its purpose is to reduce communication traffic from the device to server by offloading some of the work to the devices, we go from having devices that simply gather information and send it to the hub to having each device run cloud analytics and custom business logic.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/manage-iot-devices?u=76281980&t=191)** Azure IOT Edge is made up of three components.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/manage-iot-devices?u=76281980&t=194)** The runtime runs on each IOT Edge device and manages the modules deployed to each device.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/manage-iot-devices?u=76281980&t=200)** The modules are the runtime code for the device.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/manage-iot-devices?u=76281980&t=203)** The dashboard provides an interface to manage your devices.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/manage-iot-devices?u=76281980&t=206)** For example, deploy new modules to all the factory floor cameras.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/manage-iot-devices?u=76281980&t=210)** In order for code to run on the device, there has to be a custom runtime engine installed.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/manage-iot-devices?u=76281980&t=215)** Once it's on the device, it handles all of these tasks.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/manage-iot-devices?u=76281980&t=218)** It installs and updates workloads on the server.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/manage-iot-devices?u=76281980&t=221)** It maintains security standards on the device.
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/manage-iot-devices?u=76281980&t=223)** It ensures that modules are always running.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/manage-iot-devices?u=76281980&t=226)** It reports module health to the cloud for remote monitoring and it manages communication between the Azure service and any downstream Leaf devices.

#### Azure Arc: Unify multicloud and on-premises management
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] A hybrid cloud is a computing environment that compliance an on-premises data center, also called a private cloud with a public cloud.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=8)** Over 85% of enterprises use a hybrid approach because it allows data and applications to live where they need to.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=16)** It's common for companies to have legacy data centers or hardware that can't or won't be moved to the public cloud, yet these private resources often need to integrate with the public cloud parts.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=27)** Whether or not the private and public cloud services are integrated, no one wants to work with multiple management tools.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=34)** Companies want one tool to manage their hybrid clouds.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=38)** Microsoft knows this and has released several hybrid cloud management tools.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=42)** Azure Arc is the newest hybrid management tool.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=45)** It replaces the prior Azure stack and Azure Pack tools.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=49)** Azure Arc is a set of offerings that allow you to bring Azure management anywhere.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=54)** It extends Azure management features to resources not hosted within Azure, such as Kubernetes clusters, virtual machines, and more.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=62)** With Azure Arc, you can use familiar tools and management practices to take care of these resources across data centers, edge environments, and multi-cloud setups.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=73)** Azure Arc collaborates with Azure Resource Manager, also called ARM, by providing a centralized, unified way to manage your entire environment.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=83)** Here's how it works.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=84)** Azure Arc allows you to project your existing non-Azure and on-premises resources into Azure Resource Manager.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=91)** When you project a resource, you essentially create a representation of it in Azure Resource Manager.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=97)** This representation includes metadata, tags and other relevant information.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=102)** By doing this, you can manage these resources alongside your Azure resources as if they were all running in Azure.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=110)** To clarify, Azure Resource Manager manages the system.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=114)** This is the tools that you would use to manage your native Azure Cloud resources.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=118)** Azure Arc brings private cloud infrastructure to Azure Resource Manager.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=123)** There is no need to use this unless you want to manage non Azure resources from the Azure Management tools.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=129)** Azure Resource Manager is the deployment and management service for Azure.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=133)** It provides a management layer that enables you to create, update, and delete resources in your Azure account.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=139)** This is where you can control access and security, automate management tasks, configure environments, control resource inventory, and organize assets, and it ensures your systems meets governance and compliance standards.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=154)** The first tip to Arc enabling the infrastructure is by installing one or more Azure Arc agents in your private ecosystem.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=161)** The agent connects and synchronizes the private cloud to the Azure portal.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=166)** This provides a consistent way to manage all environments and apply uniform policies, security and monitoring.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=172)** As I said, Arc enabled infrastructure appears in the Azure portal alongside native Azure infrastructure.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=179)** The point of Azure Arc is that it works with the hardware or cloud providers you already have.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=184)** You can communicate with Azure through three routes, a user interface, a command line interface, and an API.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/azure-arc-unify-multi-cloud-and-on-premises-management?u=76281980&t=190)** It's good to know that Azure Arc supports these via the Azure portal, the Azure CLI, and the Azure REST API.

#### Back up and recover data with Azure Backup
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/backup-and-recover-data-with-azure-backup?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/backup-and-recover-data-with-azure-backup?u=76281980&t=9)** There are several backup agents and services available.

>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/backup-and-recover-data-with-azure-backup?u=76281980&t=44)** For Azure virtual machines, you get independent and isolated backups to guard against accidental destruction of original data.

>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/backup-and-recover-data-with-azure-backup?u=76281980&t=72)** Azure Backup can also backup on-premises items, not just data you have stored in the Azure Cloud.

>

>

>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/backup-and-recover-data-with-azure-backup?u=76281980&t=130)** It's a way to start utilizing the benefits of cloud technology like cost savings and scalability, for your backup strategy.

>

>

>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/backup-and-recover-data-with-azure-backup?u=76281980&t=160)** Hybrid environments often require mixed storage, some on-premises and some in the cloud.

>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/backup-and-recover-data-with-azure-backup?u=76281980&t=169)** Azure Backup automatically allocates and manages backup storage, and it uses a pay-as-you-use model, so you only pay for the storage you consume.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/backup-and-recover-data-with-azure-backup?u=76281980&t=177)** To conclude our look at Azure Backup, it is a cloud-based solution for simple, secure and cost-effective data backup services.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/backup-and-recover-data-with-azure-backup?u=76281980&t=183)** It can be used to backup data from different platforms to Azure.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/backup-and-recover-data-with-azure-backup?u=76281980&t=187)** It eliminates the need for additional infrastructure for backing up virtual machines and SQL servers, and maintains data and application consistency.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/backup-and-recover-data-with-azure-backup?u=76281980&t=195)** With the Azure Central Backup Management Portal, it is easy to manage resources and restore data when needed.

>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=127)** If you're considering lift and shift migrations, this service is ideal for you.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=132)** Azure Resource Graph is a powerful service designed for efficient exploration of Azure resources across multiple subscriptions.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=139)** While it may not be necessary for single subscription setups, it is invaluable for enterprise environments.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=145)** It supports complex querying using Kusto Query Language, making it ideal for managing large scale environments with intricate resource configurations.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=154)** It extends Azure Resource Management by providing seamless access to properties from resource providers, eliminating the need for individual calls.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=163)** Azure Blueprints is a service that helps cloud architects and IT teams define repeatable sets of Azure resources, ensuring they meet organizational standards and requirements.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=173)** It supports quick and consistent deployment of resources with built-in components like networking to speed up development.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=179)** Azure Blueprints is declarative, orchestrating the deployment of resource templates and other artifacts like role assignments, policy assignments, Azure Resource Manager templates and resource groups.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=190)** It's backed by Azure Cosmos DB, which offers low latency, high availability, and consistent access to blueprint objects.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=198)** Unlike Azure Resource Manager templates, Azure Blueprints maintains the relationship between the blueprint definition and its assignment, allowing for better tracking and auditing of deployments.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=208)** It can also upgrade multiple subscriptions governed by the same blueprint.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=212)** One important note, Azure Blueprints will be depreciated in 2026.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=218)** It's advisable to migrate existing blueprint definitions and assignments to the template specs and the deployment stacks.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=224)** Azure now has a system for working with orbital satellites.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=228)** It's called Azure Orbital, a ground station as a service product, that allows organizations with satellites and spacecraft to communicate with and process data from those crafts without having to own a satellite ground station.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=240)** Azure Digital Twins is an IOT platform that enables you to create digital representations of real world entities such as things, places, business processes, and people.
>
> **[4:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=251)** These environments can include buildings, factories, farms, energy networks, railways, and stadiums.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=257)** It is designed to work seamlessly with the other Azure IOT services providing a comprehensive way to virtually represent and manage the physical world in a digital space.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=267)** Is that all the services available?
>
> **[4:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=269)** Not at all.
>
> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=271)** The list we've explored today is far from exhaustive.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=273)** Microsoft continually expands and enhances Azure, offering more innovative services with Azure.
>
> **[4:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-understanding-the-big-picture-24392017/the-rest-of-the-services?u=76281980&t=280)** There's always something new to learn and explore.
